lang="en">North America</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>\n<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"North American" redirects here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/North_American_(disambiguation)" title="North American (disambiguation)">North American (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Northern_America" title="Northern America">Northern America</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Continent entirely within the Northern Hemisphere and almost all within the Western Hemisphere</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><caption>North America</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" &#8211; North America<br/><code>019</code> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a><br/><code>001</code> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/World" title="World">World</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>North America</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continent</a> entirely within the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a> and almost all within the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>; it is also considered by some to be a northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subcontinent" title="Subcontinent">subcontinent</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica-northamerica_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-northamerica-4">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup> It is bordered to the north by the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic Ocean</a>, to the east by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, to the west and south by the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, and to the southeast by <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>.\n</p><p>North America covers an area of about 24,709,000 square kilometers (9,540,000 square miles), about 16.5% of the <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">earth\'s</a> land area and about 4.8% of its total surface.\nNorth America is the third largest continent by area, following <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_continents_by_population" title="List of continents by population">fourth</a> by population after Asia, Africa, and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> In 2013, its population was estimated at nearly 579 million people in <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_North_America" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories in North America">23 independent states</a>, or about 7.5% of the world\'s population, if nearby islands (most notably the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>) are included.\n</p><p>North America was reached by its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prehistoric_migration_and_settlement_of_the_Americas_from_Asia" title="Prehistoric migration and settlement of the Americas from Asia">first human populations</a> during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a>, via crossing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bering_land_bridge" title="Bering land bridge">Bering land bridge</a> approximately 40,000 to 17,000 years ago. The so-called <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">Paleo-Indian</a> period is taken to have lasted until about 10,000 years ago (the beginning of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaic_period_in_North_America" title="Archaic period in North America">Archaic or Meso-Indian</a> period). The <a href="/wiki/Classic_stage" title="Classic stage">Classic stage</a> spans roughly the 6th to 13th centuries. The <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">Pre-Columbian era</a> ended in 1492, and the <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_migrations" title="Transatlantic migrations">transatlantic migrations</a>&#8212;the arrival of European settlers during the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Modern_period" title="Early Modern period">Early Modern period</a>. Present-day cultural and ethnic patterns reflect different kinds of interactions between <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous peoples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">African slaves</a> and their descendants.\n</p><p>Owing to the European colonization of the Americas, most North Americans speak English, Spanish or French, and their culture commonly reflects <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western traditions</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historisch_Nordamerika.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="314" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Historisch_Nordamerika.jpg/330px-Historisch_Nordamerika.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/dc/Historisch_Nordamerika.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historisch_Nordamerika.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of North America, from 1621</div></div></div>\n<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">The Americas</a> are usually accepted as having been named after the Italian explorer <a href="/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci" title="Amerigo Vespucci">Amerigo Vespucci</a> by the German cartographers <a href="/wiki/Martin_Waldseem%C3%BCller" title="Martin Waldseem&#252;ller">Martin Waldseem&#252;ller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Ringmann" title="Matthias Ringmann">Matthias Ringmann</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> Vespucci, who explored South America between 1497 and 1502, was the first <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> to suggest that the Americas were not the <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a>, but a different landmass previously unknown by Europeans. In 1507, Waldseem&#252;ller produced a world map, in which he placed the word "America" on the continent of South America, in the middle of what is today Brazil. He explained the rationale for the name in the accompanying book <i>Cosmographiae Introductio</i>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<blockquote><p><i lang="la" title="Latin language text">... ab Americo inventore ... quasi Americi terram sive Americam</i> (from Americus the discoverer ... as if it were the land of Americus, thus America).</p></blockquote>\n<p>For Waldseem&#252;ller, no one should object to the naming of the land after its discoverer. He used the Latinized version of Vespucci\'s name (Americus Vespucius), but in its feminine form "America", following the examples of "Europa", "Asia" and "Africa". Later, other mapmakers extended the name <i>America</i> to the northern continent, In 1538, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gerard_Mercator" title="Gerard Mercator">Gerard Mercator</a> used <i>America</i> on his map of the world for all the Western Hemisphere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cohen_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-10">[9]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some argue that because the convention is to use the surname for naming discoveries (except in the case of royalty), the derivation from "Amerigo Vespucci" could be put in question.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> In 1874, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Belt" title="Thomas Belt">Thomas Belt</a> proposed a derivation from the <a href="/wiki/Amerrisque_Mountains#Origin_of_the_name_America" title="Amerrisque Mountains"><i>Amerrique</i> mountains</a> of Central America; the next year, <a href="/wiki/Jules_Marcou" title="Jules Marcou">Jules Marcou</a> suggested that the name of the mountain range stemmed from <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">indigenous American languages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> Marcou corresponded with <a href="/wiki/Augustus_Le_Plongeon" title="Augustus Le Plongeon">Augustus Le Plongeon</a>, who wrote: "The name AMERICA or AMERRIQUE in the <a href="/wiki/Mayan_languages" title="Mayan languages">Mayan language</a> means, a country of perpetually strong wind, or the Land of the Wind, and ... the [suffixes] can mean ... a spirit that breathes, life itself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cohen_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen-10">[9]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Extent"><span id="Usage_of_the_term">Extent</span></span></h2>\n<p>The United Nations formally recognizes "North America" as comprising three areas: Northern America, Central America, and The Caribbean. This has been formally defined by the UN Statistics Division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The term <i>North America</i> maintains various definitions in accordance with location and context. In <a href="/wiki/Canadian_English" title="Canadian English">Canadian English</a>, <i>North America</i> generally refers to the land mass as a whole consisting of Mexico, the United States, and Canada, although it is generally ambiguous which other countries are included, and is mostly defined by context.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> In the United States of America, usage of the term may refer only to Canada and the US, and sometimes includes <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAGreenland_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIAGreenland-19">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CountryReports_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-CountryReports-20">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eNotes_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-eNotes-21">[20]</a></sup> and Mexico (as in the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CountryReports_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-CountryReports-20">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trilateral_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trilateral-22">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spp_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-spp-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epa_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-epa-24">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-About.com_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-About.com-25">[24]</a></sup> as well as offshore islands.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, and the countries of Latin America, the <a href="/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">cognates</a> of <i>North America</i> usually designate a subcontinent of the Americas comprising Canada, the United States, and Mexico, and often Greenland, Saint Pierre et Miquelon, and Bermuda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p>North America has been historically referred to by other names. Spanish North America (<a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>) was often referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Northern_America" title="Northern America">Northern America</a></i>, and this was the <a href="/wiki/Solemn_Act_of_the_Declaration_of_Independence_of_Northern_America" title="Solemn Act of the Declaration of Independence of Northern America">first official name</a> given to Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AGN_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-AGN-31">[30]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_Canada" title="List of regions of Canada">List of regions of Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_regions_of_the_United_States" title="List of regions of the United States">List of regions of the United States</a></div>\n<p>Geographically the North American continent has many regions and subregions. These include cultural, economic, and geographic regions. Economic regions included those formed by trade blocs, such as the North American Trade Agreement bloc and Central American Trade Agreement. Linguistically and culturally, the continent could be divided into <a href="/wiki/Anglo-America" title="Anglo-America">Anglo-America</a> and Latin America. Anglo-America includes most of Northern America, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, and Caribbean islands with English-speaking populations (though sub-national entities, such as <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, have large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francophone" title="Francophone">Francophone</a> populations; in Quebec, French is the sole official language<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-language_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-language-32">[31]</a></sup>).\n</p><p>The southern North American continent is composed of two regions. These are Central America and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BritannicaCA_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-BritannicaCA-33">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> The north of the continent maintains recognized regions as well. In contrast to the common definition of "North America", which encompasses the whole continent, the term "North America" is sometimes used to refer only to Mexico, Canada, the United States, and Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAGreenland_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIAGreenland-19">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CountryReports_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-CountryReports-20">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eNotes_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-eNotes-21">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trilateral_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Trilateral-22">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The term Northern America refers to the northern-most countries and territories of North America: the United States, Bermuda, St. Pierre and Miquelon, Canada and Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> Although the term does not refer to a unified region,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Middle_America_(Americas)" title="Middle America (Americas)">Middle America</a>&#8212;not to be confused with the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwestern United States</a>&#8212;groups the regions of Mexico, Central America, and the Caribbean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest countries of the continent, Canada and the United States, also contain well-defined and recognized regions. In the case of Canada these are (from east to west) <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic Canada</a>, Central Canada, <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Prairies" title="Canadian Prairies">Canadian Prairies</a>, the <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia_Coast" title="British Columbia Coast">British Columbia Coast</a>, and Northern Canada. These regions also contain many subregions. In the case of the United States &#8211; and in accordance with the US Census Bureau definitions &#8211; these regions are: <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_states" title="Mid-Atlantic states">Mid-Atlantic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_States" title="South Atlantic States">South Atlantic States</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_North_Central_States" title="East North Central States">East North Central States</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_North_Central_States" title="West North Central States">West North Central States</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_South_Central_States" title="East South Central States">East South Central States</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_South_Central_States" title="West South Central States">West South Central States</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountain_States" title="Mountain States">Mountain States</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_States" title="Pacific States">Pacific States</a>. Regions shared between both nations included the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_region_(North_America)" title="Great Lakes region (North America)">Great Lakes Region</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megalopolis_(city_type)" title="Megalopolis (city type)">Megalopolises</a> have formed between both nations in the case of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">Pacific Northwest</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Megaregion" title="Great Lakes Megaregion">Great Lakes Megaregion</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Flag_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Flag_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Flag_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Turks_and_Caicos_Islands.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span>\n</td>\n<td><a
