//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/NYC_wideangle_south_from_Top_of_the_Rock.jpg/400px-NYC_wideangle_south_from_Top_of_the_Rock.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><center><a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a></center></div></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_North_American_countries_by_population" title="List of North American countries by population">List of North American countries by population</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_North_American_cities_by_population" title="List of North American cities by population">List of North American cities by population</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_North_American_metropolitan_areas_by_population" title="List of North American metropolitan areas by population">List of North American metropolitan areas by population</a></div>\n<p>The most populous country in North America is the United States with 329.7 million persons. The second largest country is Mexico with a population of 112.3 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INEGI_2010_Census_Statistics_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-INEGI_2010_Census_Statistics-116">[107]</a></sup> Canada is the third most populous country with 37.0 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[108]</a></sup> The majority of Caribbean island-nations have national populations under a million, though Cuba, Dominican Republic, Haiti, Puerto Rico (a territory of the United States), Jamaica, and Trinidad and Tobago each have populations higher than a million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cubastat_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-cubastat-118">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prez_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-prez-119">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[113]</a></sup> Greenland has a small population of 55,984 for its massive size (2,166,000&#160;km&#178; or 836,300&#160;mi&#178;), and therefore, it has the world\'s lowest population density at 0.026 pop./km&#178; (0.067 pop./mi&#178;).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[114]</a></sup>\n</p><p>While the United States, Canada, and Mexico maintain the largest populations, large city populations are not restricted to those nations. There are also large cities in the Caribbean. The largest cities in North America, by far, are Mexico City and New York. These cities are the only cities on the continent to exceed eight million, and two of three in the Americas. Next in size are Los Angeles, <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[115]</a></sup> Chicago, Havana, Santo Domingo, and <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>. Cities in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunbelt" title="Sunbelt">sunbelt</a> regions of the United States, such as those in Southern California and <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix</a>, Miami, <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas</a>, are experiencing rapid growth. These causes included warm temperatures, retirement of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baby_Boomers" title="Baby Boomers">Baby Boomers</a>, large industry, and the influx of immigrants. Cities near the United States border, particularly in Mexico, are also experiencing large amounts of growth. Most notable is <a href="/wiki/Tijuana" title="Tijuana">Tijuana</a>, a city bordering San Diego that receives immigrants from all over Latin America and parts of Europe and Asia. Yet as cities grow in these warmer regions of North America, they are increasingly forced to deal with the major issue of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_shortages" title="Water shortages">water shortages</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[116]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Eight of the top ten <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_areas" title="Metropolitan areas">metropolitan areas</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Table_of_United_States_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="Table of United States Metropolitan Statistical Areas">are located in the United States</a>. These metropolitan areas all have a population of above 5.5 million and include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_City_metropolitan_area" title="New York City metropolitan area">New York City metropolitan area</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area" title="Los Angeles metropolitan area">Los Angeles metropolitan area</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_metropolitan_area" title="Chicago metropolitan area">Chicago metropolitan area</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Dallas&#8211;Fort Worth metroplex">Dallas&#8211;Fort Worth metroplex</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstCBSA_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstCBSA-126">[117]</a></sup> Whilst the majority of the largest metropolitan areas are within the United States, Mexico is host to the largest metropolitan area by population in North America: <a href="/wiki/Greater_Mexico_City" title="Greater Mexico City">Greater Mexico City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[118]</a></sup> Canada also breaks into the top ten largest metropolitan areas with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toronto_metropolitan_area" title="Toronto metropolitan area">Toronto metropolitan area</a> having six million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statcan2006_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-statcan2006-128">[119]</a></sup> The proximity of cities to each other on the <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Canada&#8211;United States border">Canada&#8211;United States border</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="Mexico&#8211;United States border">Mexico&#8211;United States border</a> has led to the rise of international metropolitan areas. These <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_agglomerations" title="Urban agglomerations">urban agglomerations</a> are observed at their largest and most productive in <a href="/wiki/Detroit%E2%80%93Windsor" title="Detroit&#8211;Windsor">Detroit&#8211;Windsor</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Diego%E2%80%93Tijuana" title="San Diego&#8211;Tijuana">San Diego&#8211;Tijuana</a> and experience large commercial, economic, and cultural activity. The metropolitan areas are responsible for millions of dollars of trade dependent on international freight. In Detroit-Windsor the Border Transportation Partnership study in 2004 concluded US$13 billion was dependent on the Detroit&#8211;Windsor international border crossing while in San Diego-Tijuana freight at the Otay Mesa Port of Entry was valued at US$20 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Planning_SD-TJ_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Planning_SD-TJ-130">[121]</a></sup>\n</p><p>North America has also been witness to the growth of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megapolitan_area" title="Megapolitan area">megapolitan areas</a>. In the United States exists eleven megaregions that transcend international borders and comprise Canadian and Mexican metropolitan regions. These are the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Sun_Corridor" title="Arizona Sun Corridor">Arizona Sun Corridor</a>, Cascadia, Florida, <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range</a>, Great Lakes Megaregion, <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="Gulf Coast of the United States">Gulf Coast Megaregion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northeast_megalopolis" title="Northeast megalopolis">Northeast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_California" title="Northern California">Northern California</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piedmont_Atlantic" title="Piedmont Atlantic">Piedmont Atlantic</a>, Southern California, and the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Triangle" title="Texas Triangle">Texas Triangle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[122]</a></sup> Canada and Mexico are also the home of megaregions. These include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quebec_City_%E2%80%93_Windsor_Corridor" title="Quebec City &#8211; Windsor Corridor">Quebec City &#8211; Windsor Corridor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horseshoe" title="Golden Horseshoe">Golden Horseshoe</a> &#8211; both of which are considered part of the Great Lakes Megaregion &#8211; and megalopolis of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Central_Mexico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Central Mexico (page does not exist)">Central Mexico</a>. Traditionally the largest megaregion has been considered the Boston-Washington, DC Corridor, or the Northeast, as the region is one massive contiguous area. Yet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_megapolitan_areas#Megaregions_and_planning:_A_brief_history" title="United States megapolitan areas">megaregion criterion</a> have allowed the Great Lakes Megalopolis to maintain status as the most populated region, being home to 53,768,125 people in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPA08_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-RPA08-132">[123]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The top ten largest North American <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan areas</a> by population as of 2013, Salvador</a></td>\n<td>25,855</td>\n<td>2018\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>North America\'s GDP per capita was evaluated in October 2016 by the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF) to be $41,830, making it the richest continent in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFcapitaGDP_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-IMFcapitaGDP-2">[1]</a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-us_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-cia-us-133">[124]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Canada, Mexico, and the United States have significant and multifaceted economic systems. The United States has the largest economy of all three countries and in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-us_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia-us-133">[124]</a></sup> In 2016, the U.S. had an estimated per capita gross domestic product (PPP) of $57,466 according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, and is the most technologically developed economy of the three.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[125]</a></sup> The United States\' services sector comprises 77% of the country\'s GDP (estimated in 2010), industry comprises 22% and agriculture comprises 1.2%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-us_133-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia-us-133">[124]</a></sup> The U.S. economy is also the fastest growing economy in North America and the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> as a whole,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFcapitaGDP_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-IMFcapitaGDP-2">[1]</a></sup> with the highest GDP per capita in the Americas as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFcapitaGDP_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-IMFcapitaGDP-2">[1]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Canada shows significant growth in the sectors of services, mining and manufacturing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-ca_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-cia-ca-136">[127]</a></sup> Canada\'s per capita GDP (PPP) was estimated at $44,656 and it had the 11th largest GDP (nominal) in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-ca_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia-ca-136">[127]</a></sup> Canada\'s services sector comprises 78% of the country\'s GDP (estimated in 2010), industry comprises 20% and agriculture comprises 2%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-ca_136-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia-ca-136">[127]</a></sup> Mexico has a per capita GDP (PPP) of $16,111 and as of 2014 is the 15th largest GDP (nominal) in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imf-mx_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-imf-mx-137">[128]</a></sup> Being a <a href="/wiki/Newly_industrialized_country" title="Newly industrialized country">newly industrialized country</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIA_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-AIA-94">[85]</a></sup> Mexico maintains both modern and outdated industrial and agricultural facilities and operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-mex_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-cia-mex-138">[129]</a></sup> Its main sources of income are oil, industrial exports, manufactured goods, electronics, heavy industry, automobiles, construction, food, banking and financial services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[130]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The North American economy is well defined and structured in three main economic areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UANL_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-UANL-140">[131]</a></sup> These areas are the North American Free Trade Agreement (NAFTA), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community_and_Common_Market" title="Caribbean Community and Common Market">Caribbean Community and Common Market</a> (CARICOM), and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American_Common_Market" title="Central American Common Market">Central American Common Market</a> (CACM).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UANL_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-UANL-140">[131]</a></sup> Of these trade blocs, the United States takes part in two. In addition to the larger trade blocs there is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canada-Costa_Rica_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Canada-Costa Rica Free Trade Agreement">Canada-Costa Rica Free Trade Agreement</a> among numerous other free trade relations, often between the larger, more developed countries and Central American and Caribbean countries.\n</p><p>The North America Free Trade Agreement (NAFTA) forms one of the four largest trade blocs in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[132]</a></sup> Its implementation in 1994 was designed for economic homogenization with hopes of eliminating barriers of trade and foreign investment between Canada, the United States and Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[133]</a></sup> While Canada and the United States already conducted the largest bilateral trade relationship &#8211; and to present day still do &#8211; in the world and <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_trade_relations" title="Canada&#8211;United States trade relations">Canada&#8211;United States trade relations</a> already allowed trade without national taxes and tariffs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[134]</a></sup> NAFTA allowed Mexico to experience a similar <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duty-free" title="Duty-free">duty-free</a> trade. The free trade agreement allowed for the elimination of tariffs that had previously been in place on United States-Mexico trade. Trade volume has steadily increased annually and in 2010, surface trade between the three NAFTA nations reached an all-time historical increase of 24.3% or US$791 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[135]</a></sup> The NAFTA trade bloc GDP (PPP) is the world\'s largest with US$17.617 trillion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[136]</a></sup> This is in part attributed to the fact that the economy of the United States is the world\'s largest national economy; the country had a nominal GDP of approximately $14.7 trillion in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bea2011_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-bea2011-146">[137]</a></sup> The countries of NAFTA are also some of each other\'s largest trade partners. The United States is the largest trade partner of Canada and Mexico;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[138]</a></sup> while Canada and Mexico are each other\'s third largest trade partners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[140]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Caribbean trade bloc &#8211; CARICOM &#8211; came into agreement in 1973 when it was signed by 15 Caribbean nations. As of 2000, CARICOM trade volume was US$96 billion. CARICOM also allowed for the creation of a <a href="/wiki/CARICOM_passport" title="CARICOM passport">common passport</a> for associated nations. In the past decade the trade bloc focused largely on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Free Trade Agreement">Free Trade Agreements</a> and under the CARICOM Office of Trade Negotiations (OTN) free trade agreements have been signed into effect.\n</p><p>Integration of Central American economies occurred under the signing of the Central American Common Market agreement in 1961; this was the first attempt to engage the nations of this area into stronger financial cooperation. Recent implementation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Central American Free Trade Agreement">Central American Free Trade Agreement</a> (CAFTA) has left the future of the CACM unclear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[141]</a></sup> The Central American Free Trade Agreement was signed by five Central American countries, the Dominican Republic, and the United States. The focal point of CAFTA is to create a free trade area similar to that of NAFTA. In addition to the United States, Canada also has relations in Central American trade blocs. Currently under proposal, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canada_%E2%80%93_Central_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Canada &#8211; Central American Free Trade Agreement">Canada &#8211; Central American Free Trade Agreement</a> (CA4) would operate much the same as CAFTA with the United States does.\n</p><p>These nations also take part in inter-continental trade blocs. Mexico takes a part in the <a href="/wiki/G3_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="G3 Free Trade Agreement">G3 Free Trade Agreement</a> with Colombia and Venezuela and has a trade agreement with the EU. The United States has proposed and maintained trade agreements under the <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_Free_Trade_Area" title="Transatlantic Free Trade Area">Transatlantic Free Trade Area</a> between itself and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US-Middle_East_Free_Trade_Area" title="US-Middle East Free Trade Area">US-Middle East Free Trade Area</a> between numerous Middle Eastern nations and itself; and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-Pacific_Strategic_Economic_Partnership" title="Trans-Pacific Strategic Economic Partnership">Trans-Pacific Strategic Economic Partnership</a> between Southeast Asian nations, Australia, and New Zealand.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport"><span id="Infrastructure">Transport</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_North_America" title="Transportation in North America">Transportation in North America</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PanAmericanHwy.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1828" data-file-width="1325" decoding="async" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/PanAmericanHwy.png/220px-PanAmericanHwy.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/PanAmericanHwy.png/330px-PanAmericanHwy.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/PanAmericanHwy.png/440px-PanAmericanHwy.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PanAmericanHwy.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The full <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pan_American_Highway" title="Pan American Highway">Pan American Highway</a> (including South America), from <a href="/wiki/Prudhoe_Bay,_Alaska" title="Prudhoe Bay, Alaska">Prudhoe Bay, Alaska</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ushuaia" title="Ushuaia">Ushuaia</a>, Argentina</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pan-American_Highway" title="Pan-American Highway">Pan-American Highway</a> route in the Americas is the portion of a network of roads nearly 48,000&#160;km (30,000&#160;mi) in length which travels through the mainland nations. No definitive length of the Pan-American Highway exists because the US and Canadian governments have never officially defined any specific routes as being part of the Pan-American Highway, and Mexico officially has many branches connecting to the US border. However, the total length of the portion from Mexico to the northern extremity of the highway is roughly 26,000&#160;km (16,000&#160;mi).\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Class1rr.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Class1rr.png/220px-Class1rr.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Class1rr.png/330px-Class1rr.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Class1rr.png/440px-Class1rr.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Class1rr.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2006 map of the North American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_I_railroad" title="Class I railroad">Class I railroad</a> network</div></div></div>\n<p>The First Transcontinental Railroad in the United States was built in the 1860s, linking the railroad network of the eastern US with California on the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> coast. Finished on 10 May 1869 at the famous <a href="/wiki/Golden_spike" title="Golden spike">golden spike</a> event at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Promontory_Summit,_Utah" title="Promontory Summit, Utah">Promontory Summit, Utah</a>, it created a nationwide mechanized transportation network that revolutionized the population and economy of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._West" title="U.S. West">American West</a>, catalyzing the transition from the <a href="/wiki/Wagon_train" title="Wagon train">wagon trains</a> of previous decades to a modern transportation system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-151">[142]</a></sup> Although an accomplishment, it achieved the status of first transcontinental railroad by connecting myriad eastern US railroads to the Pacific and was not the largest single railroad system in the world. The Canadian <a href="/wiki/Grand_Trunk_Railway" title="Grand Trunk Railway">Grand Trunk Railway</a> (GTR) had, by 1867, already accumulated more than 2,055&#160;km (1,277&#160;mi) of track by connecting Ontario with the Canadian Atlantic provinces west as far as <a href="/wiki/Port_Huron,_Michigan" title="Port Huron, Michigan">Port Huron, Michigan</a>, through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sarnia,_Ontario" title="Sarnia, Ontario">Sarnia, Ontario</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span></h3>\n<p>A shared telephone system known as the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Numbering_Plan" title="North American Numbering Plan">North American Numbering Plan</a> (NANP) is an integrated <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">telephone numbering plan</a> of 24 countries and territories: the United States and its <a href="/wiki/Insular_area" title="Insular area">territories</a>, Canada, Bermuda, and 17 <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> nations.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<p>Canada and the United States were both <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">former British colonies</a>. There is frequent cultural interplay between the United States and English-speaking Canada. Greenland shares some cultural ties with the indigenous people of Canada but is considered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nordic_Countries" title="Nordic Countries">Nordic</a> and has strong Danish ties due to <a href="/wiki/Danish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Danish colonization of the Americas">centuries of colonization by Denmark</a>. Spanish-speaking North America shares a common past as former <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish colonies</a>. In Mexico and the Central American countries where civilizations like the Maya developed, indigenous people preserve traditions across modern boundaries. Central American and Spanish-speaking Caribbean nations have historically had more in common due to geographical proximity.\n</p><p>Northern Mexico, particularly in the cities of <a href="/wiki/Monterrey" title="Monterrey">Monterrey</a>, Tijuana, <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Ju%C3%A1rez" title="Ciudad Ju&#225;rez">Ciudad Ju&#225;rez</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mexicali" title="Mexicali">Mexicali</a>, is strongly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States" title="Culture of the United States">culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_way" title="American way">way of life of the United States</a>. Of the aforementioned cities, Monterrey has been regarded as the most <a href="/wiki/Americanization" title="Americanization">Americanized</a> city in Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MonterreyFall_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-MonterreyFall-152">[143]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">Immigration to the United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Canada" title="Immigration to Canada">Canada</a> remains a significant attribute of many nations close to the southern border of the US. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglophone_Caribbean" title="Anglophone Caribbean">Anglophone Caribbean states</a> have witnessed the decline of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> and its influence on the region, and its replacement by the economic influence of Northern America. In the Anglophone Caribbean. This is partly due to the relatively small populations of the English-speaking Caribbean countries, and also because many of them now have more people <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">living abroad</a> than those remaining at home. Northern Mexico, the Western United States and <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, Canada share a <a href="/wiki/Cowboy" title="Cowboy">cowboy</a> culture.\n</p>\n<h3><span World Cup bid">joint bid to host</a> the <a href="/wiki/2026_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2026 FIFA World Cup">2026 FIFA World Cup</a>.\nThe following table shows the most prominent sports leagues in North
